## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (deterministic rate laws / concentration ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations. With only A and t available, plausible models are empirical/mechanistic rate laws dA_dt = f(A,t) capturing reaction order, sources/sinks, relaxation to equilibrium, and time-dependent rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption, e.g., catalyst-saturated or constant flux removal)
- Constant source with first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (chemostat-like inflow/outflow or generation plus linear degradation)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like decay, simple irreversible reaction)
- Equilibrium relaxation (linear): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- n-th order power-law kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (effective reaction order c1, lumped kinetics)
- Second-order (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with identical reactant A + A -> products)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-enhancing growth with depletion/limitation)
- Mixed-order (sum of pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel unimolecular and bimolecular consumption channels)
- Self-inhibition via rational factor: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate suppression at high A due to inhibition/crowding/limited active sites)
- Diffusion/transport-limited effective order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**0.5 (fractional-order kinetics from heterogeneous/diffusion control)
- Time-dependent first-order coefficient (e.g., temperature/programmed conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant increases/decreases exponentially in time)
- Periodic forcing/modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (photochemical or externally driven oscillatory input/removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- dA_dt proportional to A (linear in A) suggests a single dominant unimolecular loss mechanism with a constant rate coefficient.
- A**n dependence (n != 1) indicates effective reaction order from multi-body collisions, radical chain mechanisms, or lumped/empirical kinetics.
- Presence of both A and A**2 terms (or multiple powers) often implies parallel pathways or competing mechanisms active over different concentration regimes.
- A steady-state offset form (A - c1) implies relaxation toward an equilibrium/controlled setpoint concentration rather than decay to zero.
- An additive constant term in dA_dt indicates an external source/sink (feed, generation, background loss) independent of A.
- Explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient (e.g., exp(c*t), polynomial in t) indicates changing conditions (temperature ramps, catalyst activation/deactivation, light intensity schedules).
- Rational suppression factors like 1/(1 + c*A) indicate self-inhibition/limited capacity effects where increases in A reduce the per-molecule reactivity.
- Fractional powers of A (e.g., A**0.5) can reflect diffusion-limited uptake, heterogeneous surfaces, or geometry/transport constraints.
- Periodic terms in t (sin/cos) suggest externally imposed modulation (illumination cycles, stirring/flow oscillations) rather than intrinsic kinetics.

**GT: -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)**

Key observations about the GT:
- It has an A² term (polynomial)
- It has a sin(√A) term
- No dependence on t
- No linear A term, no constant term, no log terms

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I need to check if each candidate can produce exactly `-c0*A² + c2*sin(√A)` for some choice of constants.

**Critical insight:** sin(√A) is a very specific basis function. Most candidates don't contain sin(√A). Let me identify which candidates could potentially produce sin(√A).

For sin(√A), I need sin of √A. Let me check candidates with sin() or log() terms:

- sin(c*log(c*|A|+1)): This is sin of a logarithm, NOT sin(√A). These are fundamentally different functions.
- log(c*exp(A*c)+1): This is a softplus-like function, not sin(√A).
- sin(A*c + c): This is sin of a linear function, not sin(√A).

**No candidate contains sin(√A) explicitly.** Let me check if any transformation could yield sin(√A):

Could `sin(c3*log(c4*|A|+1))` equal `sin(√A)`? This requires `c3*log(c4*A+1) = √A` for all A≥0. But log(c4*A+1) and √A are linearly independent functions - they have different functional forms. No constants can make log equal to √A for all A.

Could `cos(c3 + c4*log(c5*|A|+1))` work? Same issue - log ≠ √A.

Let me check every candidate systematically for the presence of sin(√A) or equivalent:

Going through all 64 candidates, none of them contain `sin(sqrt(A))` as a term or any combination that could produce it. The sin terms present use arguments like:
- `c*log(c*|A|+1)` (Candidates 8,9,10,36,39,40,55)
- `A*c + c` (Candidates 31,33,42,45,60,61)
- `c*t + c` (Candidates 43)

None of these can equal √A for all A.

The log-based candidates (2,3,11,26,28,29,34,37, etc.) use log(cA+1) which is also not equivalent to sin(√A).

The polynomial candidates (7,21,22) use half-integer powers of A but no sin function.

For candidates with t-dependence, I can set t-coefficients to 0, but that doesn't help create sin(√A).

Let me verify: Is there ANY candidate that has sin(√A) or could produce it? After careful review of all 64 candidates - **none** contain sin(√A) or any functional form that could be algebraically equivalent to sin(√A).

Therefore, no candidate matches.
